In Europe in particular, ethnic minorities have had their rights undermined by populism, while in Latin America it is political opposition groups who have been undermined by populist governments.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201784_259-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201784-259">[259]</a></sup>

In several instances—such as Orban in Hungary—the populist leader has set the country on a path of de-democratisation by changing the constitution to centralise increasing levels of power in the head of government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201791_253-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201791-253">[253]</a></sup> A December 2018 study of 46 populist leaders argued that populists, regardless of their position on the political spectrum, were more likely to damage democratic institutions, erode checks and balances on the executive branch, cause [democratic backsliding](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_backsliding "Democratic backsliding") and attack individual rights than non-populists.<sup id="cite_ref-260"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup> In contrast, an analysis of the [V-Party Dataset](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/V-Dem_Institute#V-Party_Dataset "V-Dem Institute") demonstrates moderate levels of populism are not necessarily antidemocratic, only high levels of populism are related to higher [autocratization](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autocratization "Autocratization").<sup id="cite_ref-Medzihorsky_Lindberg_2023_50-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-Medzihorsky_Lindberg_2023-50">[50]</a></sup>

Even when not elected into office, populist parties can have an impact in shaping the national political agenda; in Western Europe, parties like the French National Front and Danish People's Party did not generally get more than 10 or 20% of the national vote, but mainstream parties shifted their own policies to meet the populist challenge.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201798_261-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201798-261">[261]</a></sup>

### Mainstream responses [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Populism&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Mainstream responses")

Mudde and Rovira Kaltwasser suggested that to deflate the appeal of populism, those government figures found guilty of corruption need to be seen to face adequate punishment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017110_262-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017110-262">[262]</a></sup> They also argued that stronger [rule of law](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule_of_law "Rule of law") and the elimination of systemic corruption were also important facets in preventing populist growth.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017111_263-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017111-263">[263]</a></sup> They believed that mainstream politicians wishing to reduce the populist challenge should be more open about the restrictions of their power, noting that those who backed populist movements were often frustrated with the dishonesty of established politicians who "claim full agency when things go well and almost full lack of agency when things go wrong".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017112_264-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017112-264">[264]</a></sup> They also suggested that the appeal of populism could be reduced by wider civic education in the values of liberal democracy and the relevance of pluralism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017112_264-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017112-264">[264]</a></sup>

What Mudde and Rovira Kaltwasser believed was ineffective was a full-frontal attack on the populists which presented "them" as "evil" or "foolish", for this strategy plays into the binary division that populists themselves employ.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017116_247-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017116-247">[247]</a></sup> In their view, "the best way to deal with populism is to engage—as difficult as it is—in an open dialogue with populist actors and supporters" in order to "better understand the claims and grievances of the populist elites and masses and to develop liberal democratic responses to them".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017118_265-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017118-265">[265]</a></sup>

> In trying to win over populist supporters, and perhaps even some elites, liberal democrats should avoid both simplistic solutions that pander to "the people" and elitist discourses that dismiss the moral and intellectual competence of ordinary citizens – both will only strengthen the populists. Most importantly, given that populism often asks the right questions but provides the wrong answers, the ultimate goal should be not just the destruction of populist supply, but also the weakening of populist demand. Only the latter will actually strengthen liberal democracy.

Political scientists Mudde and Rovira Kaltwasser<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017118_265-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017118-265">[265]</a></sup>

Mainstream politicians have sometimes sought to co-operate or build alliances with populists. In the United States, for example, various Republican Party figures aligned themselves with the Tea Party movement, while in countries such as Finland and Austria populist parties have taken part in governing coalitions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017113_266-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017113-266">[266]</a></sup> In other instances, mainstream politicians have adopted elements of a populist political style while competing against populist opponents.<sup id="cite_ref-267"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> Various mainstream centrist figures, such as [Hillary Clinton](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hillary_Clinton "Hillary Clinton") and [Tony Blair](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_Blair "Tony Blair"), have argued that governments needed to restrict migration to hinder the appeal of right-wing populists utilising anti-immigrant sentiment in elections.<sup id="cite_ref-268"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-269"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup>

A more common approach has been for mainstream parties to openly attack the populists and construct a _[cordon sanitaire](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cordon_sanitaire_(politics) "Cordon sanitaire (politics)")_ to prevent them from gaining political office <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017113_266-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017113-266">[266]</a></sup> Once populists are in political office in liberal democracies, the judiciary can play a key role in blocking some of their more illiberal policies, as has been the case in Slovakia and Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017114_270-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017114-270">[270]</a></sup> The mainstream media can play an important role in blocking populist growth; in a country like Germany, the mainstream media is for instant resolutely anti-populist, opposing populist groups whether left or right.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017114_270-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017114-270">[270]</a></sup> Mudde and Rovira Kaltwasser noted that there was an "odd love-hate relationship between populist media and politicians, sharing a discourse but not a struggle".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017115_271-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017115-271">[271]</a></sup>

In certain countries, certain mainstream media outlets have supported populist groups; in Austria, the _Kronen Zeitung_ played a prominent role in endorsing Haider, in the United Kingdom the _[Daily Express](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daily_Express "Daily Express")_ supported the [UK Independence Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/UK_Independence_Party "UK Independence Party"), while in the United States, [Fox News](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fox_News "Fox News") gave much positive coverage and encouragement to the Tea Party movement.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017114_270-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017114-270">[270]</a></sup> In some cases, when the populists have taken power, their political rivals have sought to violently overthrow them; this was seen in the [2002 Venezuelan coup d'état attempt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_Venezuelan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt "2002 Venezuelan coup d'état attempt"), when mainstream groups worked with sectors of the military to unseat Hugo Chávez's government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017113_266-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017113-266">[266]</a></sup>

Another discursive strategy of mainstream parties dealing with populist actors is demonization.<sup id="cite_ref-272"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-273"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup> However, Schwörer and Fernández-García found that this practice is less common in Western Europe as usually assumed and that the center-right even refuses to harshly attack the populist radical right.<sup id="cite_ref-274"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup> In a similar vein, mainstream parties use the term "populism" to delegitimize populist actors due to its negative connotation among the public but also use the term to attack non-populist competitors.<sup id="cite_ref-275"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup>

### [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Populism&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Authoritarianism")

Scholars have argued that populist elements have sometimes appeared in [authoritarian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarianism "Authoritarianism") movements.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerkiss1957_276-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerkiss1957-276">[276]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDobratzShanks–Meile1988_277-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDobratzShanks%E2%80%93Meile1988-277">[277]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerletLyons2000_278-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerletLyons2000-278">[278]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFritzsche1990_279-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFritzsche1990-279">[279]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-281"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup> Some, but not all, populists are authoritarian, emphasizing "the importance of protecting [traditional](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditionalist_conservatism "Traditionalist conservatism") lifestyles against perceived threats from 'outsiders', even at the expense of civil liberties and [minority rights](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minority_rights "Minority rights")."<sup id="cite_ref-Norris2_282-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-Norris2-282">[282]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1987-0410-503,_N%C3%BCrnberg,_Reichsparteitag,_Wehrmachts-Aufmarsch.jpg)

[Nazi Party rally](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuremberg_Rally "Nuremberg Rally") in [Nuremberg](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuremberg "Nuremberg"), 1936

The historian [Roger Eatwell](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Eatwell "Roger Eatwell") noted that "major ideological differences ... lie at the core" of fascism and populism, the former being anti-democratic and latter being rooted in democracy, "albeit not liberal democracy".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017381_283-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017381-283">[283]</a></sup> However, he says that fascist politicians have "borrowed aspects of populist discourse and style".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017363_284-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017363-284">[284]</a></sup> Some fascists have for instance used the terms "people" and "nation" synonymously.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017369_285-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017369-285">[285]</a></sup> The historian Peter Fritzsche argued that populist movements active in [Weimar Germany](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weimar_Germany "Weimar Germany") helped to facilitate the environment in which the fascist [Nazi Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Party "Nazi Party") could rise to power,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFritzsche1990149–150_286-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFritzsche1990149%E2%80%93150-286">[286]</a></sup> and that the Nazis utilised, "at least rhetorically", the "populist ideal of the people's community".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFritzsche1990233–235_287-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFritzsche1990233%E2%80%93235-287">[287]</a></sup> The scholar Luke March argued that the populist [Narodnik](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narodnik "Narodnik") movement of late 19th-century Russia influenced the radical rejection on the constitutional limits of the state found in [Marxism–Leninism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism "Marxism–Leninism").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarch200765_134-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarch200765-134">[134]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Stay_on_topic" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles"><span title="The material near this tag may contain information that is not relevant to the article's main topic. (May 2024)">relevant?</span></a></i>]</sup> Although the Marxist–Leninist movement often used populist rhetoric—in the 1960s, the [Communist Party of the Soviet Union](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Communist Party of the Soviet Union") called itself the "party of the Soviet people"—in practice its emphasis on an elite vanguard is anti-populist in basis.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarch200765–66_288-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarch200765%E2%80%9366-288">[288]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Stay_on_topic" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles"><span title="The material near this tag may contain information that is not relevant to the article's main topic. (May 2024)">relevant?</span></a></i>]</sup>

In recent history, a 2018 analysis by political scientists [Yascha Mounk](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yascha_Mounk "Yascha Mounk") and Jordan Kyle links populism to democratic backsliding, showing that since 1990, five out of 13 elected right-wing populist governments and five out of 15 elected left-wing populist governments brought about significant democratic backsliding.<sup id="cite_ref-289"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-289">[289]</a></sup> From the left, the [pink tide](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pink_tide "Pink tide") spreading over Latin America was "prone to populism and authoritarianism".<sup id="cite_ref-ISBESTER_290-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-ISBESTER-290">[290]</a></sup> Correa in Ecuador<sup id="cite_ref-291"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup> and [Hugo Chávez](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez "Hugo Chávez") in Venezuela and his regional allies<sup id="cite_ref-292"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEde_la_Torre2017202_187-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEde_la_Torre2017202-187">[187]</a></sup> used populism to achieve their dominance and later established authoritarian regimes when they were empowered. Such actions, Weyland argues, proves that populism is a strategy for winning and exerting state power and stands in tension with democracy and the values of pluralism, open debate, and fair competition.<sup id="cite_ref-JODweyland_293-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-JODweyland-293">[293]</a></sup>

In 2019, [Pippa Norris](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pippa_Norris "Pippa Norris") and [Ronald Inglehart](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Inglehart "Ronald Inglehart") classified over 50 European political parties as 'authoritarian-populist' as well as world leaders like [Donald Trump](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump "Donald Trump"), [Silvio Burlesconi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silvio_Berlusconi "Silvio Berlusconi"), [Viktor Orbán](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n "Viktor Orbán"), [Hugo Chávez](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez "Hugo Chávez"), [Nicholas Maduro](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicol%C3%A1s_Maduro "Nicolás Maduro"), [Jair Bolsonaro](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jair_Bolsonaro "Jair Bolsonaro"), [Narendra Modi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narendra_Modi "Narendra Modi"), and [Rodrigo Duterte](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rodrigo_Duterte "Rodrigo Duterte").<sup id="cite_ref-:4_294-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-:4-294">[294]</a></sup> They described the combination of authoritarian values disguised in populist rhetoric as perhaps the most dangerous threat to liberal democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-295"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup> They also argue that authoritarian-populism provides a more powerful analytical lens than conventional labels like [right-wing populism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right-wing_populism "Right-wing populism").<sup id="cite_ref-296"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup>

## History [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Populism&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: History")

> Although the term "populist" can be traced back to _populares_ (courting the people) Senators in Ancient Rome, the first political movements emerged during the late nineteenth century. However, some of the movements that have been portrayed as progenitors of modern populism did not develop a truly populist ideology. It was only with the coming of Boulangism in France and the American People's Party, which was also known as the Populist Party, that the foundational forms of populism can fully be discerned. In particular, it was during this era that terms such as "people" and "popular sovereignty" became a major part of the vocabulary of insurgent political movements that courted mass support among an expanding electorate by claiming that they uniquely embodied their interests\[.\]

Political historian Roger Eatwell<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017365–366_297-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017365%E2%80%93366-297">[297]</a></sup>

Mudde and Rovira Kaltwasser argue that populism is a modern phenomenon.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201721_298-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201721-298">[298]</a></sup> However, attempts have been made to identify manifestations of populism in the democracy of classical Athens.<sup id="cite_ref-299"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup> Eatwell noted that although the actual term _populism_ parallels that of the _[Populares](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populares "Populares")_ who were active in the [Roman Republic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Republic "Roman Republic"), these and other pre-modern groups "did not develop a truly populist ideology."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017365_300-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017365-300">[300]</a></sup> The origins of populism are often traced to the late nineteenth century, when movements calling themselves _populist_ arose in both the United States and the Russian Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017365MuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201721_301-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017365MuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201721-301">[301]</a></sup> Populism has often been linked to the spread of [democracy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy "Democracy"), both as an idea and as a framework for governance.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201721_298-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201721-298">[298]</a></sup>

Conversely, the historian [Barry S. Strauss](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barry_S._Strauss "Barry S. Strauss") argued that populism could also be seen in the ancient world, citing the examples of the fifth-century B.C. Athens and [Populares](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populares "Populares"), a political faction active in the [Roman Republic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Republic "Roman Republic") from the second century BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-302"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup> The historian Rachel Foxley argued that the [Levellers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levellers "Levellers") of 17th-century England could also be labelled "populists", meaning that they believed "equal natural rights ... must shape political life"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFoxley2013207_303-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFoxley2013207-303">[303]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (June 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> while the historian Peter Blickle linked populism to the [Protestant Reformation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protestant_Reformation "Protestant Reformation").<sup id="cite_ref-304"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-305"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup>

### Europe [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Populism&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Europe")

#### 19th and 20th centuries [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Populism&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: 19th and 20th centuries")

In the Russian Empire during the late 19th century, the _[narodnichestvo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narodnichestvo "Narodnichestvo")_ movement emerged, championing the cause of the empire's peasantry against the governing elites.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201732_306-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201732-306">[306]</a></sup> The movement was unable to secure its objectives; however, it inspired other agrarian movements across eastern Europe in the early 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201733_307-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201733-307">[307]</a></sup> Although the Russian movement was primarily a movement of the middle class and intellectuals "going to the people", in some respects their agrarian populism was similar to that of the US People's Party, with both presenting small farmers (the peasantry in Europe) as the foundation of society and main source of societal morality.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201733_307-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201733-307">[307]</a></sup> According to Eatwell, the narodniks "are often seen as the first populist movement".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017366_16-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017366-16">[16]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Arrest_of_a_Propagandist.jpg)

[Ilya Repin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilya_Repin "Ilya Repin")'s painting, _Arrest of a Propagandist_ (1892), which depicts the arrest of a narodnik

In German-speaking Europe, the [völkisch movement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/V%C3%B6lkisch_movement "Völkisch movement") has often been characterised as populist, with its exultation of the German people and its anti-elitist attacks on capitalism and Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017366_16-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017366-16">[16]</a></sup> In France, the [Boulangist movement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georges_Ernest_Boulanger "Georges Ernest Boulanger") also utilised populist rhetoric and themes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017366–367_308-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEatwell2017366%E2%80%93367-308">[308]</a></sup> In the early 20th century, adherents of both [Marxism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxism "Marxism") and [fascism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascism "Fascism") flirted with populism, but both movements remained ultimately elitist, emphasising the idea of a small elite who should guide and govern society.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201733_307-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201733-307">[307]</a></sup> Among Marxists, the emphasis on [class struggle](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_struggle "Class struggle") and the idea that the working classes are affected by [false consciousness](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/False_consciousness "False consciousness") are also antithetical to populist ideas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201733_307-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201733-307">[307]</a></sup>

After 1945 populism was largely absent from Europe, in part due to the domination of elitist Marxism–Leninism in Eastern Europe and a desire to emphasise moderation among many West European political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201733–34_309-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201733%E2%80%9334-309">[309]</a></sup> However, over the coming decades, a number of right-wing populist parties emerged throughout the continent.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2004548_310-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2004548-310">[310]</a></sup> These were largely isolated and mostly reflected a conservative agricultural backlash against the centralisation and politicisation of the agricultural sector then occurring.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201734_311-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201734-311">[311]</a></sup> These included [Guglielmo Giannini](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guglielmo_Giannini "Guglielmo Giannini")'s [Common Man's Front](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Common_Man%27s_Front "Common Man's Front") in 1940s Italy, [Pierre Poujade](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre_Poujade "Pierre Poujade")'s [Union for the Defense of Tradesmen and Artisans](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_for_the_Defense_of_Tradesmen_and_Artisans "Union for the Defense of Tradesmen and Artisans") in late 1950s France, [Hendrik Koekoek](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hendrik_Koekoek "Hendrik Koekoek")'s [Farmers' Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farmers%27_Party_(Netherlands) "Farmers' Party (Netherlands)") of the 1960s Netherlands, and [Mogens Glistrup](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mogens_Glistrup "Mogens Glistrup")'s [Progress Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Progress_Party_(Denmark) "Progress Party (Denmark)") of 1970s Denmark.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2004548_310-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2004548-310">[310]</a></sup> Between the late 1960s and the early 1980s there also came a concerted populist critique of society from Europe's [New Left](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Left "New Left"), including from the [new social movements](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_social_movements "New social movements") and from the early [Green parties](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_politics "Green politics").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2004548March200766_312-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2004548March200766-312">[312]</a></sup> However it was only in the late 1990s, according to Mudde and Rovira Kaltwasser, that populism became "a relevant political force in Europe", one which could have a significant impact on mainstream politics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201734_311-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201734-311">[311]</a></sup>

Following the [fall of the Soviet Union](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_the_Soviet_Union "Fall of the Soviet Union") and the [Eastern Bloc](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc") of the early 1990s, there was a rise in populism across much of Central and Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201735_313-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201735-313">[313]</a></sup> In the first multiparty elections in many of these countries, various parties portrayed themselves as representatives of "the people" against the "elite", representing the old governing Marxist–Leninist parties.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201736_314-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201736-314">[314]</a></sup> The Czech [Civic Forum](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civic_Forum "Civic Forum") party for instance campaigned on the slogan "Parties are for party members, Civic Forum is for everybody".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201736_314-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201736-314">[314]</a></sup> Many populists in this region claimed that a "real" revolution had not occurred during the transition from Marxist–Leninist to liberal democratic governance in the early 1990s and that it was they who were campaigning for such a change.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201737_315-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201737-315">[315]</a></sup>

The collapse of Marxism–Leninism as a central force in socialist politics also led to a broader growth of left-wing populism across Europe, reflected in groups like the [Dutch Socialist Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_Socialist_Party "Dutch Socialist Party"), [Scottish Socialist Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scottish_Socialist_Party "Scottish Socialist Party"), and German's [The Left](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Left_(Germany) "The Left (Germany)") party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarch200767_316-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarch200767-316">[316]</a></sup> Since the late 1980s, populist experiences emerged in Spain around the figures of [José María Ruiz Mateos](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Ruiz_Mateos "José María Ruiz Mateos"), [Jesús Gil](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jes%C3%BAs_Gil "Jesús Gil") and [Mario Conde](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mario_Conde "Mario Conde"), businessmen who entered politics chiefly to defend their personal economic interests, but by the turn of the millennium their proposals had proved to meet a limited support at the ballots at the national level.<sup id="cite_ref-317"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup>

#### 21st century [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Populism&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: 21st century")

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Right-wing_populist_parties_in_European_national_parliaments_(October_2019).png)

European national parliaments with representatives from right-wing populist parties in July 2023:<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>  
 Right-wing populists represented in the parliament  
 Right-wing populists providing external support for government  
 Right-wing populists involved in the government  
 Right-wing populists appoint prime minister/president

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Jean_Marie_LePen.jpg)

[Jean-Marie Le Pen](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean-Marie_Le_Pen "Jean-Marie Le Pen"), founder and leader of the [French National Front](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_National_Front "French National Front"), the "prototypical radical right party" which used populism to advance its cause<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201734–35_318-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201734%E2%80%9335-318">[318]</a></sup>

At the turn of the 21st century, populist rhetoric and movements became increasingly apparent in Western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2004550AlbertazziMcDonnell20082_319-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2004550AlbertazziMcDonnell20082-319">[319]</a></sup> Populist rhetoric was often used by opposition parties. For example, in [the 2001 electoral campaign](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001_United_Kingdom_general_election "2001 United Kingdom general election"), the Conservative Party leader [William Hague](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Hague "William Hague") accused [Tony Blair](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_Blair "Tony Blair")'s governing [Labour Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK) "Labour Party (UK)") government of representing "the condescending liberal elite". Hague repeatedly referring to it as "metropolitan", implying that it was out of touch with "the people", who in Conservative discourse are represented by "Middle England".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2004550_320-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2004550-320">[320]</a></sup> Blair's government also employed populist rhetoric; in outlining legislation to curtail [fox hunting](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fox_hunting "Fox hunting") on [animal welfare](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal_welfare "Animal welfare") grounds, it presented itself as championing the desires of the majority against the upper-classes who engaged in the sport.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2004551_321-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2004551-321">[321]</a></sup> Blair's rhetoric has been characterised as the adoption of a populist style rather than the expression of an underlying populist ideology.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBangMarsh2018354_322-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBangMarsh2018354-322">[322]</a></sup>

By the 21st century, European populism<sup id="cite_ref-323"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-323">[323]</a></sup> was again associated largely with the political right.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2004549_81-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2004549-81">[81]</a></sup> The term came to be used in reference both to [radical right](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radical_right_(Europe) "Radical right (Europe)") groups like Jörg Haider's FPÖ in Austria and Jean-Marie Le Pen's FN in France, as well as to non-radical right-wing groups like [Silvio Berlusconi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silvio_Berlusconi "Silvio Berlusconi")'s [Forza Italia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forza_Italia "Forza Italia") or [Pim Fortuyn](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pim_Fortuyn "Pim Fortuyn")'s LPF in the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2004549_81-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2004549-81">[81]</a></sup> The populist radical right combined populism with authoritarianism and nativism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201734_311-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201734-311">[311]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-324"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup>

Conversely, the Great Recession also resulted in the emergence of left-wing populist groups in parts of Europe, most notably the [Syriza](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syriza "Syriza") party which gained political office in Greece and the Podemos party in Spain, displaying similarities with the US-based Occupy movement.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201737_315-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201737-315">[315]</a></sup> Like Europe's right-wing populists, these groups also expressed [Eurosceptic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurosceptic "Eurosceptic") sentiment towards the European Union, albeit largely from a socialist and anti-austerity perspective rather than the nationalist perspective adopted by their right-wing counterparts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201737_315-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201737-315">[315]</a></sup> Populists have entered government in many countries across Europe, both in coalitions with other parties as well by themselves, Austria and Poland are examples of these respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-325"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup>

The UK [Labour Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK) "Labour Party (UK)") under the leadership of [Jeremy Corbyn](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeremy_Corbyn "Jeremy Corbyn") has been called populist,<sup id="cite_ref-Labour_plans_Jeremy_Corbyn_relaunch_to_ride_anti-establishment_wave_326-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-Labour_plans_Jeremy_Corbyn_relaunch_to_ride_anti-establishment_wave-326">[326]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Could_Corbyn_trigger_the_next_populist_political_earthquake?_327-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-Could_Corbyn_trigger_the_next_populist_political_earthquake?-327">[327]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Labour_is_running_a_great_risk_with_its_populist_turn_328-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-Labour_is_running_a_great_risk_with_its_populist_turn-328">[328]</a></sup> with the slogan "for the many not the few" having been used.<sup id="cite_ref-As_Labour’s_new_dawn_fades,_populists_offer_false_promise_329-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-As_Labour%E2%80%99s_new_dawn_fades,_populists_offer_false_promise-329">[329]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Why_Jeremy_Corbyn_cannot_copy_Donald_Trump’s_populism_330-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-Why_Jeremy_Corbyn_cannot_copy_Donald_Trump%E2%80%99s_populism-330">[330]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (April 2024)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-Blair:_Failing_Tories_spend_no_time_worrying_about_the_threat_from_Labour_{{!}}_LabourList_331-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-Blair:_Failing_Tories_spend_no_time_worrying_about_the_threat_from_Labour_%7B%7B!%7D%7D_LabourList-331">[331]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (April 2024)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup>

After the [2016 UK referendum on membership of the European Union](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016 "United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016"), in which British citizens voted to leave, some have claimed the "[Brexit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brexit "Brexit")" as a victory for populism, encouraging a flurry of calls for referendums among other [EU countries](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union "Member state of the European Union") by populist political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-332"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-332">[332]</a></sup>

### North America [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Populism&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: North America")

In North America, populism has often been characterised by regional mobilisation and loose organisation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201722_333-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201722-333">[333]</a></sup> During the late 19th and early 20th centuries, populist sentiments became widespread, particularly in the western provinces of Canada, and in the southwest and Great Plains regions of the United States. In this instance, populism was combined with [agrarianism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agrarianism "Agrarianism") and often known as "prairie populism".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201723_334-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201723-334">[334]</a></sup> For these groups, "the people" were yeomen—small, independent farmers —while the "elite" were the bankers and politicians of the northeast.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201723_334-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201723-334">[334]</a></sup> In some cases, populist activists called for alliances with labor (the first national platform of the National People's Party in 1892 calling for protecting the rights of "urban workmen".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETindall196690_335-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTETindall196690-335">[335]</a></sup> In the state of Georgia in the early 1890s, [Thomas E. Watson](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_E._Watson "Thomas E. Watson") led a major effort to unite poor white farmers, and included some African-American farmers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETindall1966118_336-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTETindall1966118-336">[336]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWoodward1938_337-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWoodward1938-337">[337]</a></sup>

The [People's Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Party_(United_States) "People's Party (United States)") of the late 19th century United States is considered to be "one of the defining populist movements";<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2004548_310-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2004548-310">[310]</a></sup> its members were often referred to as the Populists at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201723_334-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201723-334">[334]</a></sup> Its radical platform included calling for the nationalisation of railways, the banning of strikebreakers, and the introduction of referendums.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECanovan198117_338-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTECanovan198117-338">[338]</a></sup> The party gained representation in several state legislatures during the 1890s, but was not powerful enough to mount a successful presidential challenge. In the [1896 presidential election](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1896_United_States_presidential_election "1896 United States presidential election"), the People's Party supported the [Democratic Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Democratic_Party_(United_States) "History of the Democratic Party (United States)") candidate [William Jennings Bryan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Jennings_Bryan "William Jennings Bryan"); after his defeat, the People's Party's support plunged.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECanovan198117–18,_44–46MuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201723_339-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTECanovan198117%E2%80%9318,_44%E2%80%9346MuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201723-339">[339]</a></sup>

Other early populist political parties in the United States included the [Greenback Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Greenback_Party "United States Greenback Party"), the [Progressive Party of 1924](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Progressive_Party_(United_States,_1924) "Progressive Party (United States, 1924)") led by [Robert M. La Follette, Sr.](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_M._La_Follette,_Sr. "Robert M. La Follette, Sr."), and the [Share Our Wealth](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Share_Our_Wealth "Share Our Wealth") movement of [Huey P. Long](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huey_P._Long "Huey P. Long") in 1933–1935.<sup id="cite_ref-340"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-340">[340]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-341"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-341">[341]</a></sup> In Canada, populist groups adhering to a [social credit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_credit "Social credit") ideology had various successes at local and regional elections from the 1930s to the 1960s, although the main [Social Credit Party of Canada](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_Credit_Party_of_Canada "Social Credit Party of Canada") never became a dominant national force.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201723–24_342-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201723%E2%80%9324-342">[342]</a></sup>

By the mid-20th century, US populism had moved from a largely [progressive](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Progressivism "Progressivism") to a largely [reactionary](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reactionary "Reactionary") stance, being closely intertwined with the [anti-communist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-communist "Anti-communist") politics of the period.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201724_343-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201724-343">[343]</a></sup> In this period, the historian [Richard Hofstadter](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Hofstadter "Richard Hofstadter") and sociologist [Daniel Bell](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daniel_Bell "Daniel Bell") compared the anti-elitism of the 1890s Populists with that of [Joseph McCarthy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_McCarthy "Joseph McCarthy").<sup id="cite_ref-mkazin1_344-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-mkazin1-344">[344]</a></sup> Although not all academics accepted the comparison between the left-wing, anti-[big business](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_business "Big business") Populists and the right-wing, anti-communist McCarthyites, the term "populist" nonetheless came to be applied to both left-wing and right-wing groups that blamed elites for the problems facing the country.<sup id="cite_ref-mkazin1_344-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-mkazin1-344">[344]</a></sup>

Some mainstream politicians in the Republican Party recognised the utility of such a tactic and adopted it; Republican President [Richard Nixon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Nixon "Richard Nixon") for instance popularised the term "[silent majority](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silent_majority "Silent majority")" when appealing to voters.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201724_343-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201724-343">[343]</a></sup> Right-wing populist rhetoric was also at the base of two of the most successful third-party presidential campaigns in the late 20th century, that of [George C. Wallace](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_C._Wallace "George C. Wallace") in [1968](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1968_United_States_presidential_election "1968 United States presidential election") and [Ross Perot](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ross_Perot "Ross Perot") in [1992](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1992_United_States_presidential_election "1992 United States presidential election").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201725_1-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201725-1">[1]</a></sup> These politicians presented a consistent message that a "liberal elite" was threatening "our way of life" and using the welfare state to placate the poor and thus maintain their own power.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201725_1-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201725-1">[1]</a></sup>

Former Oklahoma Senator [Fred R. Harris](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fred_R._Harris "Fred R. Harris"), first elected in 1964, ran unsuccessfully for the US presidency in 1972 and 1976. Harris' New Populism embraced egalitarian themes.<sup id="cite_ref-345"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-345">[345]</a></sup>

In the first decade of the 21st century, two populist movements appeared in the US, both in response to the [Great Recession](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Recession "Great Recession"): the [Occupy movement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupy_movement "Occupy movement") and the [Tea Party movement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tea_Party_movement "Tea Party movement").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201726_346-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201726-346">[346]</a></sup> The populist approach of the Occupy movement was broader, with its "people" being what it called "[the 99%](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/We_are_the_99%25 "We are the 99%")", while the "elite" it challenged was presented as both the economic and political elites.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201726–27_347-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201726%E2%80%9327-347">[347]</a></sup> The Tea Party's populism was [Producerism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Producerist "Producerist"), while "the elite" it presented was more party partisan than that of Occupy, being defined largely—although not exclusively—as the Democratic administration of President [Barack Obama](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama "Barack Obama").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201726–27_347-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201726%E2%80%9327-347">[347]</a></sup>

The [2016 presidential election](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election "2016 United States presidential election") saw a wave of populist sentiment in the campaigns of [Bernie Sanders](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bernie_Sanders_presidential_campaign,_2016 "Bernie Sanders presidential campaign, 2016") and [Donald Trump](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump_presidential_campaign,_2016 "Donald Trump presidential campaign, 2016"), with both candidates running on [anti-establishment](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-establishment "Anti-establishment") platforms in the Democratic and Republican parties, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-348"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-348">[348]</a></sup> Both campaigns criticised free trade deals such as the [North American Free Trade Agreement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement "North American Free Trade Agreement") and the [Trans-Pacific Partnership](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trans-Pacific_Partnership "Trans-Pacific Partnership").<sup id="cite_ref-349"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-349">[349]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-350"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-350">[350]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-351"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-351">[351]</a></sup> Other studies have noted an emergence of populist rhetoric and a decline in the value of prior experience in U.S. intra-party contests such as congressional primaries.<sup id="cite_ref-352"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-352">[352]</a></sup> [Nativism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nativism_(politics) "Nativism (politics)") and hostility toward immigrants (especially Muslims, Hispanics and Asians) were common features.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2012_353-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2012-353">[353]</a></sup>

### Latin America [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Populism&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Latin America")

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Javier_Milei_en_el_Sal%C3%B3n_Blanco_2_(cropped).jpg)

Javier Milei, Argentina President is a well known right wing populist

Populism has been dominant in Latin American politics since the 1930s and 1940s,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEde_la_Torre2017195_55-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEde_la_Torre2017195-55">[55]</a></sup> being far more prevalent there than in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarch200769_354-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarch200769-354">[354]</a></sup> Mudde and Rovira Kaltwasser noted that the region has the world's "most enduring and prevalent populist tradition".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201727_355-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201727-355">[355]</a></sup> They suggested that this was the case because it was a region with a long tradition of democratic governance and free elections, but with high rates of socio-economic inequality, generating widespread resentments that politicians can articulate through populism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201727–28_356-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201727%E2%80%9328-356">[356]</a></sup> March instead thought that it was the important role of "catch-all parties and prominent personalities" in Latin American politics which had made populism more common.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarch200769_354-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarch200769-354">[354]</a></sup>

The first wave of Latin American populism began at the start of the [Great Depression](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Depression "Great Depression") in 1929 and last until the end of the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201728_357-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201728-357">[357]</a></sup> In various countries, politicians took power while emphasising "the people": these included [Getúlio Vargas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Get%C3%BAlio_Vargas "Getúlio Vargas") in Brazil, [Juan Perón](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_Per%C3%B3n "Juan Perón") in Argentina, and [José María Velasco Ibarra](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Velasco_Ibarra "José María Velasco Ibarra") in Ecuador.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201728–29de_la_Torre2017196_358-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201728%E2%80%9329de_la_Torre2017196-358">[358]</a></sup> These relied on the _[Americanismo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americanismo "Americanismo")_ ideology, presenting a common identity across Latin America and denouncing any interference from [imperialist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperialism "Imperialism") powers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201729_359-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201729-359">[359]</a></sup> The second wave took place in the early 1990s;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201729de_la_Torre2017198_360-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201729de_la_Torre2017198-360">[360]</a></sup> de la Torre called it "neoliberal populism".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEde_la_Torre2017198_361-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEde_la_Torre2017198-361">[361]</a></sup>

In the late 1980s, many Latin American states were experiencing economic crisis and several populist figures were elected by blaming the elites for this situation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201729_359-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201729-359">[359]</a></sup> Examples include [Carlos Menem](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carlos_Menem "Carlos Menem") in Argentina, [Fernando Collor de Mello](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fernando_Collor_de_Mello "Fernando Collor de Mello") in Brazil, and [Alberto Fujimori](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alberto_Fujimori "Alberto Fujimori") in Peru.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201729de_la_Torre2017198_360-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201729de_la_Torre2017198-360">[360]</a></sup> Once in power, these individuals pursued neoliberal economic strategies recommended by the [International Monetary Fund](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund "International Monetary Fund") (IMF).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201729–30de_la_Torre2017199_362-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201729%E2%80%9330de_la_Torre2017199-362">[362]</a></sup> Unlike the first wave, the second did not include an emphasis on Americanismo or anti-imperialism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201731_363-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201731-363">[363]</a></sup>

The third wave began in the final years of the 1990s and continued into the 21st century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201731_363-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201731-363">[363]</a></sup> It overlapped in part with the [pink tide](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pink_tide "Pink tide") of left-wing resurgence in Latin America. Like the first wave, the third made heavy use of Americanismo and anti-imperialism, although this time these themes presented alongside an explicitly socialist programme that opposed the free market.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201731_363-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201731-363">[363]</a></sup> Prominent examples included Hugo Chávez in Venezuela, [Cristina de Kirchner](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Kirchner "Cristina Fernández de Kirchner") in Argentina, Evo Morales in Bolivia, Rafael Correa in Ecuador, and [Daniel Ortega](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daniel_Ortega "Daniel Ortega") in Nicaragua.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarch200771MuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201731de_la_Torre2017199_364-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarch200771MuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201731de_la_Torre2017199-364">[364]</a></sup> These socialist populist governments have presented themselves as giving sovereignty "back to the people", in particular through the formation of [constituent assemblies](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constituent_assembly "Constituent assembly") that would draw up new constitutions, which could then be ratified via referendums.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201732de_la_Torre2017200_365-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201732de_la_Torre2017200-365">[365]</a></sup> In this way they claimed to be correcting the problems of social and economic injustice that liberal democracy had failed to deal with, replacing it with superior forms of democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEde_la_Torre2017201_366-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEde_la_Torre2017201-366">[366]</a></sup>

### Oceania [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Populism&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Oceania")

During the 1990s, there was a growth in populism in both Australia and New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201738_367-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201738-367">[367]</a></sup>

In New Zealand, [Robert Muldoon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Muldoon "Robert Muldoon"), the [31st Prime Minister of New Zealand](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_New_Zealand "List of Prime Ministers of New Zealand") from 1975 to 1984, had been cited as a populist.<sup id="cite_ref-368"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-368">[368]</a></sup> Populism has become a pervasive trend in [New Zealand politics](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Zealand_politics "New Zealand politics") since the introduction of the [mixed-member proportional](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mixed-member_proportional "Mixed-member proportional") voting system in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-Mazzoleni_369-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-Mazzoleni-369">[369]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-370"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-370">[370]</a></sup> The [New Zealand Labour Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Zealand_Labour_Party "New Zealand Labour Party")'s populist appeals in its [1999 election](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Zealand_general_election,_1999 "New Zealand general election, 1999") campaign and advertising helped to propel the party to victory in that election.<sup id="cite_ref-Boston_371-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-Boston-371">[371]</a></sup> [New Zealand First](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Zealand_First "New Zealand First") has presented a more lasting populist platform; long-time party leader [Winston Peters](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Peters "Winston Peters") has been characterised by some as a populist who uses anti-establishment rhetoric,<sup id="cite_ref-Moore_372-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-Moore-372">[372]</a></sup> though in a uniquely New Zealand style.<sup id="cite_ref-Landis-Albert_373-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-Landis-Albert-373">[373]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-374"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-374">[374]</a></sup>

### Sub-Saharan Africa [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Populism&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Sub-Saharan Africa")

In much of Africa, populism has been a rare phenomenon.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201739_375-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201739-375">[375]</a></sup> The political scientist Danielle Resnick argued that populism first became apparent in Africa during the 1980s, when a series of coups brought military leaders to power in various countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEResnick2017102_376-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEResnick2017102-376">[376]</a></sup> In Ghana, for example, [Jerry Rawlings](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerry_Rawlings "Jerry Rawlings") took control, professing that he would involve "the people" in "the decision-making process", something he claimed had previously been denied to them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEResnick2017102_376-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEResnick2017102-376">[376]</a></sup> A similar process took place in neighbouring Burkina Faso under the military leader [Thomas Sankara](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Sankara "Thomas Sankara"), who professed to "take power out of the hands of our national bourgeoisie and their imperialist allies and put it in the hands of the people".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEResnick2017103_377-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEResnick2017103-377">[377]</a></sup> Such military leaders claimed to represent "the voice of the people", utilised an anti-establishment discourse, and established participatory organisations through which to maintain links with the broader population.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEResnick2017103–104_378-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEResnick2017103%E2%80%93104-378">[378]</a></sup>

In the 21st century, with the establishment of multi-party democratic systems in much of Sub-Saharan Africa, new populist politicians have appeared. These have included Kenya's [Raila Odinga](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raila_Odinga "Raila Odinga"), Senegal's [Abdoulaye Wade](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdoulaye_Wade "Abdoulaye Wade"), South Africa's [Julius Malema](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julius_Malema "Julius Malema"), and Zambia's [Michael Sata](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Sata "Michael Sata").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEResnick2017106_379-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEResnick2017106-379">[379]</a></sup> These populists have arisen in democratic rather than authoritarian states, and have arisen amid dissatisfaction with democratisation, socio-economic grievances, and frustration at the inability of opposition groups to oust incumbent parties.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEResnick2017106–107_380-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEResnick2017106%E2%80%93107-380">[380]</a></sup>

### Asia and the Arab world [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Populism&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Asia and the Arab world")

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:President_Rodrigo_Roa_Duterte_poses_for_a_photo_with_Indian_Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_prior_to_the_start_of_the_bilateral_meeting_at_the_Hyderabad_House_in_New_Delhi.jpg)

[Rodrigo Duterte](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rodrigo_Duterte "Rodrigo Duterte") of the [Philippines](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippines "Philippines") and [Narendra Modi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narendra_Modi "Narendra Modi") of [India](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/India "India"), 2018. They are both considered populist leaders of the left and right, respectively.

In North Africa, populism was associated with the approaches of several political leaders active in the 20th century, most notably Egypt's [Gamal Abdel Nasser](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser "Gamal Abdel Nasser") and Libya's [Muammar Gaddafi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi "Muammar Gaddafi").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201739_375-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201739-375">[375]</a></sup> However, populist approaches only became more popular in the Middle East during the early 21st century, by which point it became integral to much of the region's politics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201739_375-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201739-375">[375]</a></sup> Here, it became an increasingly common element of mainstream politics in established representative democracies, associated with longstanding leaders like Israel's [Benjamin Netanyahu](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu "Benjamin Netanyahu").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201739–40_381-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201739%E2%80%9340-381">[381]</a></sup> Although the [Arab Spring](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Spring "Arab Spring") was not a populist movement itself, populist rhetoric was present among protesters.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201740_382-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201740-382">[382]</a></sup>

In southeast Asia, populist politicians emerged in the wake of the [1997 Asian financial crisis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1997_Asian_financial_crisis "1997 Asian financial crisis"). In the region, various populist governments took power but were removed soon after: these include the administrations of [Joseph Estrada](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Estrada "Joseph Estrada") in the Philippines, [Roh Moo-hyun](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roh_Moo-hyun "Roh Moo-hyun") in South Korea, [Chen Shui-bian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chen_Shui-bian "Chen Shui-bian") in Taiwan, and [Thaksin Shinawatra](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thaksin_Shinawatra "Thaksin Shinawatra") in Thailand.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201738–39_383-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser201738%E2%80%9339-383">[383]</a></sup> In India, the [Hindu nationalist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_nationalism "Hindu nationalism") [Bharatiya Janata Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party "Bharatiya Janata Party") (BJP) which rose to increasing power in the early 21st century adopted a right-wing populist position.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcDonnellCabrera2019484_384-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDonnellCabrera2019484-384">[384]</a></sup> Unlike many other successful populist groups, the BJP was not wholly reliant on the personality of its leader, but survived as a powerful electoral vehicle under several leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcDonnellCabrera2019485_385-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDonnellCabrera2019485-385">[385]</a></sup>

### Late 20th- and early 21st-century growth [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Populism&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Late 20th- and early 21st-century growth")

[Sheri Berman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheri_Berman "Sheri Berman") reviews various explanations of populism including "demand- and supply-side explanations of populism, economic grievance–based and sociocultural grievance–based explanations of populism, and structure- and agency-based explanations of populism".<sup id="cite_ref-Berman_3-17"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-Berman-3">[3]</a></sup> There is now a wide-ranging and interdisciplinary literature in this area.<sup id="cite_ref-Berman_3-18"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-Berman-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mounk_386-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-Mounk-386">[386]</a></sup>

In the early 1990s, there was an increasing awareness of populism in established liberal democracies, sometimes referred to as the "New Populism".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECanovan2004242_193-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTECanovan2004242-193">[193]</a></sup> The UK's [referendum on European Union membership](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum "2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum") and the election of Donald Trump, both in 2016, generated a substantial rise in interest in the concept from both academics and the public.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETormey2018260_387-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTETormey2018260-387">[387]</a></sup> By 2016, "populism" was regularly used by political commentators.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnselmi20181_27-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnselmi20181-27">[27]</a></sup>

A 2017 review of votes for populistic parties in all developed countries discovered them spiking in 2015 and reaching highest levels since WWII.<sup id="cite_ref-388"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-388">[388]</a></sup>

> The rise of populism in Western Europe is, in large part, a reaction to the failure of traditional parties to respond adequately in the eyes of the electorate to a series of phenomena such as [economic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_globalization "Economic globalization") and [cultural globalisation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_globalisation "Cultural globalisation"), the speed and direction of [European integration](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_integration "European integration"), immigration, the decline of ideologies and class politics, exposure of elite corruption, etc. It is also the product of a much-cited, but rarely defined, "political malaise", manifested in steadily falling [voter turnout](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voter_turnout "Voter turnout") across Western Europe, declining [political party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_party "Political party") membership, and ever-greater numbers of citizens in surveys citing a lack of interest and distrust in politics and politicians.

Albertazzi and McDonnell, 2008<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAlbertazziMcDonnell20081_389-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAlbertazziMcDonnell20081-389">[389]</a></sup>

Mudde argued that by the early 1990s, populism had become a regular feature in Western democracies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2004551_321-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2004551-321">[321]</a></sup> He attributed this to changing perceptions of government that had spread in this period, which in turn he traced to the changing role of the media to focus increasingly on [sensationalism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sensationalism "Sensationalism") and scandals.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2004553_390-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2004553-390">[390]</a></sup> Since the late 1960s, the emergence of [television](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Television "Television") had allowed for the increasing proliferation of the Western media, with media outlets becoming increasingly independent of political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2004553_390-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2004553-390">[390]</a></sup> As private media companies have had to compete against each other, they have placed an increasing focus on scandals and other sensationalist elements of politics, in doing so promoting anti-governmental sentiments among their readership and cultivating an environment prime for populists.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2004553MuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017103–104_391-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2004553MuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017103%E2%80%93104-391">[391]</a></sup>

At the same time, politicians increasingly faced television interviews, exposing their flaws.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017108_392-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017108-392">[392]</a></sup> News media had also taken to interviewing fewer accredited experts, and instead favouring interviewing individuals found on the street as to their views about current events.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017108_392-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017108-392">[392]</a></sup> At the same time, mass media was giving less attention to the "[high culture](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_culture "High culture")" of elites and more to other sectors of society, as reflected in [reality television](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reality_television "Reality television") shows such as _[Big Brother](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_Brother_(franchise) "Big Brother (franchise)")_.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017108_392-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeRovira_Kaltwasser2017108-392">[392]</a></sup>

Mudde argued that another reason for the growth of Western populism in this period was the improved education of the populace; since the 1960s, citizens have expected more from their politicians and felt increasingly competent to judge their actions. This in turn has led to an increasingly sceptical attitude toward mainstream politicians and governing groups.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2004554_393-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2004554-393">[393]</a></sup> In Mudde's words, "More and more citizens think they have a good understanding of what politicians do, and think they can do it better."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMudde2004556_394-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMudde2004556-394">[394]</a></sup>
